King Hussein was then forced to flee to [Amman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amman "Amman"), [Transjordan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emirate_of_Transjordan "Emirate of Transjordan"), where his son [Abdullah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_I_of_Jordan "Abdullah I of Jordan") was [Emir](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emir_of_Transjordan "Emir of Transjordan"). During this period, King Hussein is described as having taken over control that his son wielded, and therefore was sent to live in [Aqaba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aqaba "Aqaba") (which was recently transferred from Hijazi to Transjordanian sovereignty by the British).<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_116-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-books.google.com-116">[115]</a></sup> Britain – responding to Ibn Saud's plea that the Sharif be expelled from Aqaba<sup id="cite_ref-117"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> – exiled him from Aqaba to [British-controlled Cyprus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/British_Cyprus_(1878%E2%80%931960) "British Cyprus (1878–1960)").<sup id="cite_ref-118"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup>

He lived in [Nicosia](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Nicosia "Nicosia") from 1925,<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> with his sons coming to visit him at some times, even if his relationships with them were strained, except for Zeid who came to visit him the most. According to the British governor of [Cyprus](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cyprus "Cyprus"), [Ronald Storrs](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ronald_Storrs "Ronald Storrs"), when he went to see Hussein, he found his son [Zeid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Zeid_bin_Hussein "Zeid bin Hussein") reading him the commentary of [al-Bukhari](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_al-Bukhari "Muhammad al-Bukhari") on the [Quran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran "Quran").<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> He rarely left his home, lived an austere lifestyle, and read the [Quran](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Quran "Quran"), religious books, he also read Arabic newspapers in the mornings.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> However, he still went to see horse-races and had brought Arabic horses in his exile that he treated "like his own family".<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-3"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> Hussein also did some interviews with the press during his exile.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-4"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> He received some visitors, such as Sheikh Fuad al-Khatib, [Muhammad Jamil Bayham](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Jamil_Bayham "Muhammad Jamil Bayham"), who wanted to write his biography, or the Jordanian poet [Mustafa Wahbi Tal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Wahbi_Tal "Mustafa Wahbi Tal"), among others.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-5"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> Hussein was ruined, but the local [Greek Cypriot](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greek_Cypriots "Greek Cypriots") and [Turkish Cypriot](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots "Turkish Cypriots") population considered him to be a very wealthy man and therefore tried to win his favors.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-6"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> Meanwhile, he was entangled in legal matters regarding property income in Egypt, among other things.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-7"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Husseinfuneral.jpg)

The funeral of Hussein in Jerusalem, 1931.

He tried to be friendly towards the various ethnic communities on the island but was particularly close to the [Armenians](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenians "Armenians") of the island, seeing them as victims, like himself, of the [Young Turks](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Young_Turks "Young Turks").<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-8"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> Hussein did not have any documented connection with the [Turkish Cypriot](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Turkish_Cypriots "Turkish Cypriots") community; though it is possible that one exists, there is no mention of him having visited a Turkish mosque in Nicosia.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-9"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> He met with the Armenian Archbishop of Nicosia in 1926 and received a warm welcome,<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-10"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> after that, he donated drums and instruments to the Armenian community of the island, including the Armenian Philharmonic Melkonian School.<sup id="cite_ref-120"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup>

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Chief_mourners_at_funeral_of_King_Hussein._His_sons_King_Ali_and_Emir_Abdullah_among_crowd_LCCN2002710418.jpg)

Chief mourners at funeral of Hussein. His sons King Ali and Emir Abdullah among crowd

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Funeral_of_King_Hussein,_Jerusalem,_the_casket_LOC_matpc.13451.jpg)

Funeral of Hussein, Jerusalem, the casket

He began to fall ill as early as 1928, but his favorite wife, [Adila Khanum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adila_Khanum "Adila Khanum"), passed away in 1929, which exacerbated his illness. She was buried at [Hala Sultan Tekke](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hala_Sultan_Tekke "Hala Sultan Tekke"), the largest Muslim shrine on the island.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-11"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> His two sons, [Ali](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_bin_Hussein,_King_of_Hejaz "Ali bin Hussein, King of Hejaz") and [Abdallah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_I_of_Jordan "Abdullah I of Jordan"), attended the funeral and started making preparations and requesting the British for his repatriation, believing that he didn't have much time left to live and that they needed to be by his side.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-12"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup>

#### Return and death [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=20 "Edit section: Return and death")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Funeral_of_King_Hussein,_Jerusalem_LOC_matpc.13456.jpg)

Funeral of Hussein, Jerusalem

As his health continued to deteriorate and as he was paralyzed by a stroke at age 79 in 1930,<sup id="cite_ref-books.google.com_116-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-books.google.com-116">[115]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> the British became increasingly inclined to send him back to the [Middle East](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Middle_East "Middle East"). They feared that his death would not only stir resentment among Arabs towards the United Kingdom but also potentially strain their relationships with the Hashemite rulers, all of whom were allies in the Middle East.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-13"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> The Saudis expressed their displeasure with rumors of Hussein's repatriation, especially after Hussein expressed his wish to be buried in Mecca, an event the Saudis feared would lead to "pro-Hashemite gatherings."<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-14"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> Eventually, the British decided to repatriate him to Amman, with Baghdad as another option they had considered.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-15"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> Upon his arrival, he was greeted by a large crowd that cheered him and followed him to the [Raghadan Palace](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raghadan_Palace "Raghadan Palace").<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-16"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup> There, while in Amman, he published a series of texts in al-Yarmouk, an Arabic newspaper, where he defended his actions and stated once again that he was against the [British mandate of Palestine](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mandate_for_Palestine "Mandate for Palestine").<sup id="cite_ref-:35_124-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:35-124">[123]</a></sup>

He died on June 4, 1931. Hussein bin Ali was buried in [Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem") in 1931, as he wasn't able to be buried in [Mecca](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mecca "Mecca"), as he wanted and as was the norm for [Sharifs of Mecca](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharif_of_Mecca "Sharif of Mecca") until then, for [Ibn Saud](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ibn_Saud "Ibn Saud") didn't want to allow him being buried there.<sup id="cite_ref-:210_125-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:210-125">[124]</a></sup> Local dignitaries and leaders wanted him to be buried in the al-Aqsa mosque compound.<sup id="cite_ref-:30_81-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:30-81">[80]</a></sup> This idea was kept and after a procession where 30,000 people took part,<sup id="cite_ref-:10_126-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:10-126">[125]</a></sup> he was buried in [Jerusalem](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jerusalem "Jerusalem"): inside the [Arghūniyya](https://commons.wikimedia.org/wiki/Category:Al-Arghuniyya "commons:Category:Al-Arghuniyya"), a building on the [Haram esh-Sharif](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haram_esh-Sharif "Haram esh-Sharif") or "[Temple Mount](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Temple_Mount "Temple Mount")", in a walled enclosure decorated with white marble and carpets.<sup id="cite_ref-127"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> His son Faisal, with whom the relationship was the worse at that point, didn't attend his funerals, claiming he had "government business" to attend to.<sup id="cite_ref-:14_119-17"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:14-119">[118]</a></sup>

On the window above his tomb is written the following inscription: [Arabic](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_language "Arabic language"): هَذَا قَبْرُ أَمِيرِ ٱلْمُؤْمِنِينَ ٱلْحُسَيْن بْنُ عَلِي, <small><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Literal_translation" title="Literal translation">lit.</a> </small> 'Haḏa qabru ʾamīri ʾal-mūˈminīna ʾal-Ḥusayn bnu ʿAlī' which translates "This is the tomb of the [Commander of the Faithful](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amir_al-Mu%27minin "Amir al-Mu'minin"), Hussein bin Ali".<sup id="cite_ref-:5_22-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:5-22">[21]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_126-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:10-126">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup>

## Marriage and children [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=21 "Edit section: Marriage and children")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:The_sons_of_Sharif_Hussein.jpg)

The sons of Sharif Hussein, King of Hejaz: King Ali of Hejaz and King Feisal I of Iraq and King Abdullah I of Transjordan

Hussein, who had four wives, fathered five sons and three daughters with three of his wives:

-   Sharifa Abidiya bint Abdullah (died Constantinople, Ottoman Empire, 1888, buried there), eldest daughter of his paternal uncle, Amir Abdullah Kamil Pasha, Grand Sharif of Mecca;
-   Madiha, a Circassian;
-   Sharifa Khadija bint Abdullah (1866 – Amman, Transjordan, 4 July 1921), second daughter of Amir Abdullah Kamil Pasha, Grand Sharif of Mecca;
-   [Adila Khanum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Adila_Khanum "Adila Khanum") (Constantinople, Ottoman Empire, 1879 – Larnaca, Cyprus, 12 July 1929, buried there at the Hala Sultan, Umm Haram, Tekke), daughter of Salah Bey and granddaughter of [Mustafa Rashid Pasha](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Re%C5%9Fid_Pasha "Mustafa Reşid Pasha"), sometime [Grand Vizier of the Ottoman Empire](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grand_Vizier_of_the_Ottoman_Empire "Grand Vizier of the Ottoman Empire");

With his first wife Abidiya bint Abdullah, he had:

-   [Prince Ali](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_of_Hejaz "Ali of Hejaz"), last King of Hejaz married to [Nafisa bint Abdullah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nafisa_bint_Abdullah&action=edit&redlink=1 "Nafisa bint Abdullah (page does not exist)"). Parents of [Aliya bint Ali](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliya_bint_Ali "Aliya bint Ali"). Grandparents of [Sharif Ali bin al-Hussein](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sharif_Ali_bin_al-Hussein "Sharif Ali bin al-Hussein").
-   Hasan bin Hussein, died young.<sup>[<i><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
-   [Prince Abdullah](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abdullah_I_of_Jordan "Abdullah I of Jordan"), Emir (later King) of Transjordan, married to [Musbah bint Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musbah_bint_Nasser "Musbah bint Nasser"), [Suzdil Hanum](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Suzdil_Hanum&action=edit&redlink=1 "Suzdil Hanum (page does not exist)"), and [Nahda bint Uman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Nahda_bint_Uman&action=edit&redlink=1 "Nahda bint Uman (page does not exist)").
-   [Princess Fatima](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Princess_Fatima_bint_Hussein&action=edit&redlink=1 "Princess Fatima bint Hussein (page does not exist)"), married a European Muslim businessman from France.
-   [Prince Faisal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_I_of_Iraq "Faisal I of Iraq"), later King of Iraq and Syria, married to [Huzaima bint Nasser](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huzaima_bint_Nasser "Huzaima bint Nasser"). Parents of [Ghazi, King of Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ghazi_of_Iraq "Ghazi of Iraq") born 1912 died 4 April 1939, married his first cousin, Princess [Aliya bint Ali](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aliya_bint_Ali "Aliya bint Ali"), daughter of [HM King Ali of Hejaz](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ali_of_Hejaz "Ali of Hejaz").

With his second wife Madiha, he had:

-   [Princess Saleha](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Princess_Saleha_bint_Hussein&action=edit&redlink=1 "Princess Saleha bint Hussein (page does not exist)"), married [Abdullah bin Muhammed](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Abdullah_bin_Muhammed&action=edit&redlink=1 "Abdullah bin Muhammed (page does not exist)").

With his third wife Adila, he had:

-   [Princess Sara](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Princess_Sara_bint_Hussein&action=edit&redlink=1 "Princess Sara bint Hussein (page does not exist)"), married [Muhammad Atta Amin](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Muhammad_Atta_Amin&action=edit&redlink=1 "Muhammad Atta Amin (page does not exist)") in July 1933, divorced September 1933.
-   [Prince Zeid](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Zeid_bin_Hussein "Prince Zeid bin Hussein"), who succeeded in pretense King [Faisal II of Iraq](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Faisal_II_of_Iraq "Faisal II of Iraq") upon his assassination in 1958, but never actually ruled as Iraq became a republic. Married to [Fahrelnissa Kabaağaç](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Princess_Fahrelnissa_Zeid "Princess Fahrelnissa Zeid").

## Works [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=22 "Edit section: Works")

### Literature [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=23 "Edit section: Literature")

Hussein wrote extensively, his most important papers were published in a book by [Prince Ghazi bin Muhammad](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Ghazi_bin_Muhammad "Prince Ghazi bin Muhammad").<sup id="cite_ref-:35_124-1"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:35-124">[123]</a></sup> Otherwise, he is known to have written a large series of articles in _[al-Qibla](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Qibla "Al Qibla")_.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEKay202078_130-0"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-FOOTNOTEKay202078-130">[129]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-131"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup>

## Legacy [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=24 "Edit section: Legacy")

### Art [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=25 "Edit section: Art")

 [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Mosqu%C3%A9e_Sharif_Hussein_bin_Ali-Aqaba.jpg)

Hussein bin Ali mosque in [Aqaba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aqaba "Aqaba")

Several poets wrote about him, including [Ahmed Shawqi](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ahmed_Shawqi "Ahmed Shawqi"), nicknamed the Prince of Poets,<sup id="cite_ref-132"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> who wrote a poem about his funerals<sup id="cite_ref-133"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> and [Mustafa Wahbi Tal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mustafa_Wahbi_Tal "Mustafa Wahbi Tal"), one of the most prominents Jordanian poets,<sup id="cite_ref-134"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> who wrote a poem about him.<sup id="cite_ref-137"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup>

### Armenian genocide [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=26 "Edit section: Armenian genocide")

His role in the support of Armenian refugees, especially during the [Armenian genocide](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armenian_genocide "Armenian genocide"), led him to be cited in 2014 and 2020 by Armenian Presidents [Serzh Sargsyan](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Serzh_Sargsyan "Serzh Sargsyan") and [Armen Sarkissian](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Armen_Sarkissian "Armen Sarkissian") as an example of tolerance and friendship between people<sup id="cite_ref-138"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-140"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> also stressed by Jordanian [Prince Hassan bin Talal](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prince_Hassan_bin_Talal "Prince Hassan bin Talal").<sup id="cite_ref-142"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> Hussein is quoted in the book _Crows of the Desert_ from Armenian survivor Levon Yotnakhparian, when he discusses the help Hussein provided to the survivors and to save victims.<sup id="cite_ref-:26_92-2"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-:26-92">[91]</a></sup> This book subsequently gave birth to a movie of the same name.<sup id="cite_ref-143"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup>

For his actions during the Armenian genocide, Hussein was awarded the title of "Righteous of the Armenian genocide" by Armenian researchers.<sup id="cite_ref-144"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> On Friday 24 April 2015, on the occasion of the centennial of the Armenian genocide, [Lebanese](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lebanon "Lebanon") Sheikh Maher Hammoud referenced Hussein ben Ali in his sermon condemning the genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-145"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup>

### Others [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=27 "Edit section: Others")

Several mosques bear his name to the present day, such as the Hussein bin Ali mosque in [Aqaba](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aqaba "Aqaba"),<sup id="cite_ref-146"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> the Hussein bin Ali mosque in [Ma'an](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ma%27an "Ma'an")<sup id="cite_ref-147"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-147">[146]</a></sup> or the al-Husseini mosque in [Amman](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Amman "Amman").<sup id="cite_ref-148"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> A school is named after him in Ma'an.<sup id="cite_ref-150"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> His house in Aqaba began to be restored in 2023 at the initiative of the Jordanian government.<sup id="cite_ref-151"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup>

In 2020, a documentary was made about him and his life by [Al-Araby](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Al_Araby_(TV_channel) "Al Araby (TV channel)"),<sup id="cite_ref-153"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> which was seen more than five million times on [YouTube](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/YouTube "YouTube") as of May 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-154"><a href="https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup>

## Decorations [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=28 "Edit section: Decorations")

-    [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Legion_Honneur_GC_ribbon.svg) Grand Cross of the [Legion of Honour](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legion_of_Honour "Legion of Honour") (France)
-    [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Order_of_the_Osmanie_lenta.png) First Class of the [Order of Osmanieh](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Osmanieh "Order of Osmanieh") (Ottoman Empire)
-    [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Order_of_the_Medjidie_lenta.png) First Class of the [Order of the Medjidie](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_the_Medjidie "Order of the Medjidie") (Ottoman Empire)
-    [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Ordre_du_Nichan_Iftikhar_GC_ribbon_(Tunisia).svg) Grand Cross of the [Order of the Nichan Iftikhar](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_Glory_(Ottoman_Empire) "Order of Glory (Ottoman Empire)") (Ottoman Empire)
-    [](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Order_of_the_Bath_UK_ribbon.svg) Knight Grand Cross of the [Order of the Bath](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Order_of_the_Bath "Order of the Bath") (United Kingdom)

## References [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=31 "Edit section: References")

### Notes [edit](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz&action=edit&section=32 "Edit section: Notes")

1.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_ref-19 "Jump up")** The legitimacy of his Caliphate is disputed; however, the date of end can be assigned to his loss of the Harayman, in 1925 or to his death, in 1931. Both interpretations can be found in sources.

13.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_ref-:8_13-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_ref-:8_13-1) Hanne, Olivier (17 November 2016). SPM (ed.). ["La révolte arabe en 1916: mythe et réalité"](https://halshs.archives-ouvertes.fr/halshs-01532691). _TELEMME – Temps, espaces, langages Europe méridionale-Méditerranée_ (in French): 331. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20221008182632/https://halshs.archives-ouvertes.fr/halshs-01532691) from the original on 8 October 2022. Retrieved 7 October 2022. Dès l'automne 1916, il commence à imprimer sa marque dans le Hejâz, puisque le corps sénatorial qu'il constitue le 7 octobre est composé notamment des muftis chafite et malékite, mais pas des représentants du rite hanafte – offciel dans l'empire ottoman – ni hanbalite – celui des wahhabites. Le 23 décembre, il se déclare indifférent à la monarchie et libre face aux puissances européennes et va jusqu'à décliner l'offre de débarquement franco-britannique (27 décembre). Son obsession reste le califat. Sa législation en est le signe puisqu'il lance la lutte contre le péché à Médine. Le 30 octobre 1916, les cafés ne peuvent rien vendre durant les heures de prières ; le 3 mai 1917, l'alcool est interdit. Il restaure en janvier 1917 les titres traditionnels arabo-musulmans (chérif, sayyid, shaykh) et abolit les titres turcs (effendi, bey, pacha…).
14.  ^ [Jump up to: <sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup>](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_ref-:9_14-0) [<sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup>](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_ref-:9_14-1) الوطن, جريدة; webmaster (5 May 2020). [""مملكة الحجاز".. وقــصـــة الـغــزو المـســلّـــح"](https://www.al-watan.com/article/230610/NEWS/%C2%AB%D9%85%D9%85%D9%84%D9%83%D8%A9-%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AD%D8%AC%D8%A7%D8%B2%C2%BB-%D9%88%D9%82%D9%80%D9%80%D8%B5%D9%80%D9%80%D9%80%D8%A9-%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%80%D8%BA%D9%80%D9%80%D8%B2%D9%88-%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%80%D8%B3%D9%80%D9%80%D9%84%D9%91%D9%80%D9%80%D9%80%D8%AD). _جريدة الوطن_ (in Arabic). [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20230516230552/https://www.al-watan.com/article/230610/NEWS/%C2%AB%D9%85%D9%85%D9%84%D9%83%D8%A9-%D8%A7%D9%84%D8%AD%D8%AC%D8%A7%D8%B2%C2%BB-%D9%88%D9%82%D9%80%D9%80%D8%B5%D9%80%D9%80%D9%80%D8%A9-%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%80%D8%BA%D9%80%D9%80%D8%B2%D9%88-%D8%A7%D9%84%D9%85%D9%80%D8%B3%D9%80%D9%80%D9%84%D9%91%D9%80%D9%80%D9%80%D8%AD) from the original on 16 May 2023. Retrieved 16 May 2023. وذكر الوثائقي أنه في 1924م، اندفع الشريف الحسين بن علي متشبثاً برداء النبوة ليعلن نفسه خليفة للمسلمين، فتلقى بيعة واسعة في الحجاز والشام، الأمر الذي زاد من غضب بن سعود، فكان إعلان الخلافة القشة التي قصمت ظهر البعير، فقرر بن سعود غزو الحجاز فوراً.

46.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_ref-47 "Jump up")** Willman, Gabriel (1 August 2013). ["From Pre-Islam to Mandate States: Examining Cultural Imperialism and Cultural Bleed in the Levant"](https://stars.library.ucf.edu/honorstheses1990-2015/1515). _Him 1990–2015_. [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20230429084719/https://stars.library.ucf.edu/honorstheses1990-2015/1515/) from the original on 29 April 2023. Retrieved 25 April 2023. When Sayyid Hussein bin Ali, the Sharif of Mecca, and the Hashemites organized an "Arab" revolt during World War II, he garnered support from across the entire region, including the Levant. By the fall of the Ottoman Empire, the Arabization of the Levant had reached the point that the traditional tribal leadership was willing to accept the rule of the Hashemite family of Arabia.

[_A Comprehensive Dictionary of the Middle East_](https://books.google.com/books?id=ty0uAgAAQBAJ). Interlink Publishing. p. 9.3500. [ISBN](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-1-62371-033-0](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-62371-033-0 "Special:BookSources/978-1-62371-033-0"). [Archived](https://web.archive.org/web/20230518102906/https://books.google.com/books?id=ty0uAgAAQBAJ) from the original on 18 May 2023. Retrieved 21 December 2023. By declaring an Arab revolt in 1916, Hussein bin Ali, the Hashemite governor of Hijaz \[q.v.\], became the leader of pan-Arabism, with a plan to see the Arab territories formed into a single independent Arab state after the defeat of the Ottomans. But this scenario contradicted the aims of the clandestine 1916 Sykes–Picot Pact \[q.v.\] signed by Britain and France.

77.  **[^](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hussein_bin_Ali,_King_of_Hejaz#cite_ref-78 "Jump up")** Le Naour, Jean-Yves (2017). _Djihad 1914–1918: la France face au panislamisme_. Paris: Perrin. [ISBN](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISBN_(identifier) "ISBN (identifier)") [978-2-262-07083-0](https://en.m.wikipedia.org/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-2-262-07083-0 "Special:BookSources/978-2-262-07083-0"). Au Hedjaz, l'émir Hussein tente de faire le ménage pour donner une image correcte de son pays. Il fait tuer les chiens galeux, tente d'assurer la sécurité sur les routes pour ne plus livrer les pèlerins aux bandits qui pullulent, et cherche à dissimuler les marchés aux esclaves qui indignent les musulmans français. Officiellement interdits par le gouvernement turc en 1908, ces marchés sont tellement ancrés dans la culture locale qu'ils se poursuivent au vu et au su de tous. On y achète un homme, une femme ou un enfant pour une somme allant de 1 000 à 3 000 F.
